## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task belongs to chemical kinetics, modeling the temporal evolution of reactant/product concentrations governed by rate laws. The relationship between dA_dt, A, and t typically reflects reaction order, mechanistic pathways (e.g., consecutive, parallel, autocatalytic), and potential time-dependent rate constant variations.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant reaction rate independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (proportional exponential decay or growth)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular collision-driven rate)
- Fractional-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (complex mechanisms or surface-mediated reactions)
- Autocatalytic rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (reaction accelerated by its own product accumulation)
- Reversible first-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (equilibrium-driven relaxation toward steady state)
- Time-modulated rate constant: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (environmental drift or catalyst deactivation)
- Competing pathways rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * A**c3 (parallel reaction mechanisms)
- Inhibition-modulated kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (substrate inhibition or competitive blocking)
- Consecutive reaction coupling: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (formation and subsequent consumption)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Equilibrium-driven relaxation → Linear deviation from steady state dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A)
- Autocatalytic runaway → Quadratic or higher-order concentration dependence dA_dt = c0 * A**n (n>1)
- Catalyst deactivation/poisoning → Multiplicative time-decay modulation dA_dt = f(A) * exp(c * t)
- Parallel competing pathways → Sum of independent power-law terms dA_dt = c1 * A**n1 + c2 * A**n2
- Diffusion-controlled regime → Time-power-law dependence dA_dt = c0 * t**c1
- Quasi-steady-state approximation → Instantaneous algebraic coupling masking intermediate dynamics
- Substrate inhibition / Crowding → Rational suppression at high concentration dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A)

Simplify: `A**2*(A*c0 + c1)/(A*c3 + 1) + c2*sin(A*c4)`
First term is rational, not polynomial `A**2`. Unless `c0=0, c3=0`, then `A**2*c1 + c2*sin(A*c4)`.
If `c3=0`, denominator is 1. Then `A**2*(A*c0 + c1) + c2*sin(A*c4) = c0*A**3 + c1*A**2 + c2*sin(A*c4)`.
Set `c0=0`. Then `c1*A**2 + c2*sin(A*c4)`. Matches GT.
So Candidate 8 matches.
Verdict: MATCH.

Rational term. Unless `c0=0`, then `A**2*c1/(A+1) + ...` Not `A**2`.
If `c0=0`, it's `c1*A**2/(A+1)`. Not polynomial. -> NO MATCH.
Wait, can `A**2*(A*c0+c1)/(A+1)` be `A**2`? Only if `A*c0+c1 = A+1`, i.e., `c0=1, c1=1`. Then it's `A**2`.
But `c0, c1` are constants. If we set `c0=1, c1=1`, then `(A+1)/(A+1) = 1`. So `A**2*1 = A**2`.
Yes! `c0=1, c1=1` makes the first term `A**2`.
Then `A**2 + c2*sin(A*c3)`. Matches GT.
So Candidate 16 matches.

GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_p*sin(c3*A)
Candidates evaluated: 53

Matched candidates: ["A**2*c0 + A*c1 + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5*exp(A*c6) + c7*cos(A*c8)", "(A**2*(A*c0 + c1) + c2*(A*c3 + 1)*sin(A*c4))/(A*c3 + 1)", "A*c0 + A*c1*(A + c2) + c3*sin(A*c4)", "(A**2*(A*c0 + c1) + c2*(A + 1)*sin(A*c3))/(A + 1)", "(A**2*(A*c0 + c1) + c2*(A + c3)*sin(A*c4))/(A + c3)", "A**3*c0 + A**2*c1 + A*c2 + A + c3*exp(A*c4) + c5*cos(A*c6)", "A**2*c0 + c1*sin(A*c2)", "A**2*c0 + A*c1 + c2*cos(A*c3) + c4*exp(c5*sin(A*c6 + c7))", "A**3*c0 + A**2*c1 + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5*exp(A*c6) + c7"]

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: -0.5637·A² + 0.1314·sin(0.7617·A)**

This is a sum of two terms: a quadratic in A (specifically -c₀·A²) and a sine term (c₂·_p·sin(c₃·A)).

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

### Candidate 1:
`(A*(A³c0 + A²c1 + A + c2 + c3*exp(Ac4) + c5*cos(Ac6)) + c7 + c8*exp(Ac4) + c9*cos(Ac6))/A`

Expanding: A³c0 + A²c1 + A + c2 + c3*exp(Ac4) + c5*cos(Ac6) + c7/A + c8*exp(Ac4)/A + c9*cos(Ac6)/A

Has terms like c7/A which can't be zeroed without making the expression undefined. Set c7=0, c8=0, c9=0: gives A³c0 + A²c1 + A + c2 + c3*exp(Ac4) + c5*cos(Ac6). Set c0=0, c3=0 (with c4 anything), then: A²c1 + A + c2 + c5*cos(Ac6). Need A coefficient = 0 and c2 = 0, but A has coefficient 1 (fixed). This "A" term has coefficient 1 which is hardcoded. Cannot be zeroed.

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 2:
`(A*c0 + c1 + (A + c2)*(A*c3 + c4 + c5*exp(A*c6) + c7*log(A*c8 + 1)))/(A*c9 + c2)`

For this to simplify, set c5=0, c7=0. Then numerator: Ac0 + c1 + (A+c2)(Ac3+c4). Denominator: Ac9+c2.

(A+c2)(Ac3+c4) = A²c3 + Ac4 + Ac2c3 + c2c4

Numerator: A²c3 + A(c0+c4+c2c3) + c1+c2c4

For this to equal (Ac9+c2)(-0.5637A² + 0.1314sin(0.7617A)), we'd need polynomial/polynomial = polynomial + sin, which requires the sin to come from somewhere. But we eliminated the transcendental terms. Without them, this is a rational function, not matching. With log or exp terms, we can't produce sin.

Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 3:
`A²c0 + Ac1 + c2*sin(Ac3 + c4) + c5*exp(Ac6) + c7*cos(Ac8)`

Set c1=0, c5=0 (or c6=0 giving c5 constant absorbed), c7=0, c4=0: A²c0 + c2*sin(Ac3). This matches GT with c0=-0.5637, c2=0.1314, c3=0.7617.

Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 4:
`Ac0 + c1*sin(Ac2 + c3) + c4*cos(c5*exp(Ac6))`

Has Ac0 (linear term), sin, and cos(exp(...)). The cos(exp) is not a standard basis function. Set c0=0, c4=0: c1*sin(Ac2+c3). Missing A² term. Can't produce A².

Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 5:
`(A*c0*(A*c1 + 1) + (A*c2 + 1)*(A*c3 + (A*c1 + 1)*(A³c4 + A + c5*exp(Ac6) + c7*cos(Ac8))))/((Ac1 + 1)(Ac2 + 1))`

Let me simplify. Let me set c2=0 to simplify denominator to (Ac1+1).

Numerator becomes: Ac0(Ac1+1) + 1·(Ac3 + (Ac1+1)(A³c4 + A + c5*exp(Ac6) + c7*cos(Ac8)))

= Ac0(Ac1+1) + Ac3 + (Ac1+1)(A³c4 + A + c5*exp(Ac6) + c7*cos(Ac8))

Dividing by (Ac1+1):

= Ac0 + Ac3/(Ac1+1) + A³c4 + A + c5*exp(Ac6) + c7*cos(Ac8)

Still has Ac3/(Ac1+1) term. Set c3=0:

= Ac0 + A³c4 + A + c5*exp(Ac6) + c7*cos(Ac8)

Has hardcoded "A" term. Set c4=0, c5=0: Ac0 + A + c7*cos(Ac8) = A(c0+1) + c7*cos(Ac8). Missing A², has cos not sin.

cos(Ac8) = sin(Ac8 + π/2), so that's fine for the trig part. But we need A², and we only have linear A. Cannot match.

Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 6:
`(A*(A²c0 + A + c1 + c2*exp(Ac3)) + c4*exp(Ac3) + c5*cos(Ac6))/A`

Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 7:
`Ac0 + c1*(A+1)² + c2*sin(A+c3) + c4*exp(Ac5)`

= Ac0 + c1(A²+2A+1) + c2*sin(A+c3) + c4*exp(Ac5)

= c1A² + A(c0+2c1) + c1 + c2*sin(A+c3) + c4*exp(Ac5)

We need c1 = -0.5637, but then constant term c1 = -0.5637 ≠ 0. GT has no constant term. The sin argument is (A+c3), but GT has sin(0.7617A). sin(A+c3) has frequency 1 in A, while GT needs frequency 0.7617. These are different functions - sin(A+c3) ≠ any_constant * sin(0.7617A + phase) for all A. Also the unwanted constant c1 can't be removed.

Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 8:
`(A²(Ac0 + c1) + c2(Ac3 + 1)*sin(Ac4))/(Ac3 + 1)`

= A²(Ac0+c1)/(Ac3+1) + c2*sin(Ac4)

For the first term: A²(Ac0+c1)/(Ac3+1) = (A³c0 + A²c1)/(Ac3+1)

Polynomial long division: A³c0/(Ac3) = A²(c0/c3). 

Let me try c0=0: A²c1/(Ac3+1) + c2*sin(Ac4). This is a rational function of A plus sin. For A²c1/(Ac3+1) to equal -0.5637A², we'd need Ac3+1 = 1, i.e., c3=0. Then it's A²c1 + c2*sin(Ac4). With c1=-0.5637, c2=0.1314, c4=0.7617. ✓

Candidate 8 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 9:
`Ac0 + (Ac1+1)(A³c2 + A + c3*exp(Ac4) + c5*cos(Ac6))`

Expanding with c1=0: Ac0 + A³c2 + A + c3*exp(Ac4) + c5*cos(Ac6)

= A³c2 + A(c0+1) + c3*exp(Ac4) + c5*cos(Ac6)

With c1≠0: (Ac1+1)(A³c2+A+c3*exp(Ac4)+c5*cos(Ac6)) = A⁴c1c2 + A²c1 + ... This gets complicated. Let me set c2=0, c3=0:

(Ac1+1)(A + c5*cos(Ac6)) = A²c1 + A + Ac1c5*cos(Ac6) + c5*cos(Ac6)

Plus Ac0: A²c1 + A(c0+1) + Ac1c5*cos(Ac6) + c5*cos(Ac6)

Need c0=-1 to zero linear term. Then: A²c1 + c5*cos(Ac6)(Ac1+1)

This gives A²c1 + c5(Ac1+1)cos(Ac6). The trig term has an A-dependent amplitude, which doesn't match GT's constant-amplitude sin. Unless c1=0, but then A² term vanishes.

Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 10:
`(Ac0 + (Ac1+1)(Ac2 + c3*sin(Ac4+c5) + c6))/(Ac1+1)`

= Ac0/(Ac1+1) + Ac2 + c3*sin(Ac4+c5) + c6

Set c0=0: Ac2 + c3*sin(Ac4+c5) + c6. This is linear + sin + constant. Missing A². 

Set c1≠0, c0≠0: Ac0/(Ac1+1) is a rational function. Can it produce A²? No - Ac0/(Ac1+1) approaches c0/c1 as A→∞, it's bounded. So total is bounded + linear + sin, can't match -0.5637A².

Candidate 10 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 11:

### Candidate 13:
`A(Ac0+c1) + c2*sin(c3*log(Ac4+1)+c5) + c6*log(c7*exp(Ac8)+1)`

= A²c0 + Ac1 + c2*sin(c3*log(Ac4+1)+c5) + c6*log(c7*exp(Ac8)+1)

### Candidate 16:
`(A²(Ac0+c1) + c2(A+1)*sin(Ac3))/(A+1)`

= A²(Ac0+c1)/(A+1) + c2*sin(Ac3)

For A²(Ac0+c1)/(A+1): if c0=0, this is A²c1/(A+1). 

Polynomial division: A²c1/(A+1) = c1(A-1) + c1/(A+1) = c1A - c1 + c1/(A+1)

This is linear + constant + 1/(A+1), not A². 

If c0≠0: (A³c0+A²c1)/(A+1). Division: A³c0/(A+1) = c0(A²-A+1) - c0/(A+1). So total rational part = c0A² + (c1-c0)A + c0 + (c1-c0-... wait let me redo.

(A³c0+A²c1)/(A+1): divide A³c0+A²c1 by (A+1).

A³c0 ÷ (A+1): quotient c0A², remainder -c0A².
So A³c0 = c0A²(A+1) - c0A².
Then -c0A² + A²c1 = A²(c1-c0).
A²(c1-c0) ÷ (A+1): quotient (c1-c0)A, remainder -(c1-c0)A.
A²(c1-c0) = (c1-c0)A(A+1) - (c1-c0)A.
Then -(c1-c0)A ÷ (A+1): quotient -(c1-c0), remainder (c1-c0).

So: c0A² + (c1-c0)A - (c1-c0) + (c1-c0)/(A+1) + c2*sin(Ac3)

This has A², A, constant, 1/(A+1), and sin terms. For GT we need only A² and sin. Set c1=c0 to zero the A, constant, and 1/(A+1) terms: c0A² + c2*sin(Ac3). ✓

With c0=-0.5637, c1=-0.5637, c2=0.1314, c3=0.7617.

Candidate 16 verdict: [MATCH]
